When `deserialize_from_file` raises a `ValueError`, the code checks if `str(e) != \"DeserializationError\"`. If it's not exactly \"DeserializationError\", it re-raises the exception (line 220).\n\nHowever, the problem is that the error message from the Rust library might not be exactly \"DeserializationError\". It could be something like \"DeserializationError: ...\" with additional details. So when a corrupted cache file is encountered, the exception is raised with a message that doesn't match exactly, causing the exception to be re-raised and crash the application.\n\nThe fix would be to check if the error message *contains* \"DeserializationError\" rather than checking for exact equality.
